Change	"All planned, temporary or permanent modifications to written approved processes, specifications or standards or to qualified / validated systems, or to safety-relevant processes or systems.
They are rated into the severity categories of minor or major based on their impact on patient safety, product quality, and data integrity:
Minor
A change is classed as minor if, as a result of its implementation, from a technical or scientific point of view any negative impact on patient safety, product quality or data integrity can be excluded.
Examples: Extending a maintenance interval, correcting the wording in change-obligatory documents.
Major
A change is classed as major if, as a result of its implementation, an impact on patient safety, product quality or data integrity is possible and cannot be excluded.
Examples: Changes to specification limits / test points, reanalysis period / storage conditions, use of a different analytical method, modification and revalidation of equipment / changes in facilities (including building and utilities) / updating SOPs / updating analytical methods.

"	MHB-005478-1
Change Control	"A planned temporary or permanent modification to a process/system. Classified as either major or minor depending on their impact on safety, product quality and data integrity."	SOP-004365-2

Cleaning Limit	"Maximum permissible limit value for the residue of a previous product in the last rinse (in mg/L). This limit value is calculated specifically for the previous product in dependence of the next product. It is measured using specific or non-specific methods. Default Cleaning Limits	"The default cleaning limits have been established to enable the release of equipment for use even when the precleaning assessment cannot be executed because the next product is not yet known.

Standard cleaning is carried out to a limit of 30 mg/L non-specific residue (in every case) and an additional 30 mg/L specific residue after an active previous product or 10 mg/L specific residue after a highly active previous product, corresponding to cleaning limit type B. However, if the active previous product has the same activity (i.e. same mechanism of action, no higher potency) as the final product resulting from the next product, then the specific limit requirement can be covered by measuring a non-specific residue (as for inactive previous products). Deviation	Departure from an approved instruction or established standard	MHB-004662-1
Deviation	"Deviations are unforeseen, unplanned events which deviate from defined processes, specifications or standards.
They are rated into the severity categories of minor, major, and critical based on their impact on patient safety, product quality, and data integrity:
Minor
A deviation is classified as minor when, from a technical and scientific point of view, a negative impact on patient safety, product quality, and data integrity can be excluded.
Examples: Maintenance interval exceeded, lack of a bracketing standard within an HPLC sequence, misspelling.
Major
A deviation is classified as major when a negative impact on patient safety, product quality, or data integrity is possible, cannot be excluded and requires further investigation and impact analysis. 
Examples: incorrect quality of raw material used in process, incorrect standard used, exceeded calibration date or acceptance criterion not met.
Critical
A deviation is classified as critical if it has a direct negative impact on patient safety, product quality, or data integrity or points to a serious systematic defect in the quality systems and hereby product already distributed to the customer may be affected or is affected. 
Examples: Foreign matter such as glass splinters / foil in the final product, OOS at the API final stage, irretrievable data loss, incorrect expiry date calculated and incorrect labeling of materials. Any retrospectively detected defect on a delivered product.
"	MHB-005478-1
Deviation	"An unplanned event within defined a processes, specification or system. This is in contrast to Changes which are planned events. Deviations are classified into categories that include critical, major, minor and batch event depending on their impact on safety, product quality and data.
Batch Event - Deviation from written procedure or an unusual event where existing GMP documentation demonstrates no adverse impact to process or product quality, the root cause is known, and no investigation is required
Minor - The deviation is not expected to negatively impact product quality or data integrity
Major ‚Äì The deviation where a direct but moderate impact on product quality or data integrity is expected. The resulting product may require further processing to meet specification. The customer may be informed
Critical ‚Äì A deviation has direct impact on product quality or data integrity. The subsequent product may require re-manufacture. The customer is always informed"	SOP-004363-2
Deviation	"An unplanned event within defined processes, specifications or systems. This is in contrast to Changes which are planned events. Deviations are classified into categories that include critical, major, minor and batch event depending on their impact on safety, product quality and data integrity (see SOP-004363 (Deviations Management))."	SOP-004365-2

Metadata	"Metadata is data that describe the attributes of other data, and provide context and meaning. Typically, these are data that describe the structure, data elements, inter-relationships and other characteristics of data. It also permits data to be attributable to an individual (or if automatically generated, to the original data source).
Metadata forms an integral part of the original record. Without metadata, the data has no meaning, therefore, the integrity of the metadata are as important as the raw data, and should be kept the same way.
Audit trails are metadata. When a system has an audit trail, it must always be switched on, and reviewed regularly."	MHB-004275-2

Out Of Trend (OOT)	R√©sultat en dehors d‚Äôune tendance connue.	SOP-004823-6
Out Of Trend (OOT) result	"A time dependent result which falls outside a prediction interval or fails a statistical process control criterion.
A trend is a sequence of temporal procedures, e.g. for the manufacture of different batches of a product. There are two types of trends:
In one case, no trend is expected, e.g. in production or when analyzing process data where everyone expects that they are under statistical control.
In the other case, a trend is expected. One typical example for that is stability testing where one expects that the content of the API reduces over the storage period, or that the quantity of impurities increases over time.
There is a fundamental difference between these two types of OOT results: indeed, in the second situation the dispersion increases over time."	MHB-005478-1

Previous Product	"The previous product is the last compound (organic raw material, intermediate or API) to be produced or processed in the equipment (‚Äúlast in‚Äù). 
Organic raw materials may count as previous products only if they contribute significantly to the chemical structure of the corresponding stage product (i.e. synthesis ""building blocks"") and their use entails a regular cleaning procedure (as defined in SOP002498).

Reagents, auxiliary chemicals or solvents do not classify as previous products, unless an equipment item was used for none of the eligible previous product options for 3 consecutive campaigns.

When determining the previous product, it is required to retrace the usage of an item of equipment back for a maximum of 3 campaigns until the last eligible previous product is reached. If an item of equipment was only used for reagents, auxiliary chemicals or solvents for 3 consecutive campaigns, then the most recent analytical result (RoE) should be selected and the article number for the respective reagent or auxiliary chemical entered in the precleaning evaluation, see SS6203B."	SOP-001153-6

Purification	"Within the context of this SOP, this includes (re)crystallizations (not indiscriminate precipitations!) and chromatographic purifications (not plug filtrations!). When determining the number of remaining purifications from the next product to the corresponding API, the independence of the counted operations must be ascertained. 
E.g.: If the next product is the precursor to the API and both the precursor and the API are isolated through crystallization and removal of the mother liquor through filtration, this counts as 2 purifications. If the API is purified first by chromatographic purification and then recrystallization, this counts as 2 purifications. The number of purifications is documented on F-002031 / F-004531.
Normally, only in-house purifications up to the Final Product are counted. Further downstream purifications (e.g. further processing by customer) can only be taken into account, if they are confirmed in writing by the customer."	SOP-001153-6

Raw Data	"Raw data is defined as the original record (data) which can be described as the first-capture of information, whether recorded on paper or electronically. Information that is originally captured in a dynamic state should remain available in that state.

Special Cause	"Quality control term for an assignable cause of variation which is not an inherent part of a process, but arises out of intermittent, unpredictable, and unstable external factors (e.g. equipment malfunction, human error‚Ä¶). These extraordinary causes are infrequent and are indicated by data points that fall outside of the limits of a control chart. As these data points are caused by process inherent factors they can be excluded from the statistical evaluation."	SOP-001014-5
Specific Residue	"Amount of residue of the previous product and other detectable compounds (known and unknown) in mg/L that is determined using a quantitative method of analysis specific to the previous product (e.g. HPLC). 
For all detectable compounds which are not the previous product the same specific limit applies as for the previous product. In this way it is prevented that starting materials or possible degradation products with comparable pharmacological activity are not taken into account. However, no corrections are made for possibly different analytical response factors. 
For the same reason, the value for the largest single peak must be used in the precleaning evaluation (analytical result column on sheet 2), unless it is known to be inactive.
For the sum of all specific residues a limit of 30 mg/L applies. 
Specific analytical methods are routinely developed for APIs and active intermediates. When a rinse result is required by W-002395 for an inactive intermediate, this is covered by measuring a non-specific residue (( worst case result).
If an item of equipment was only used for compounds which are not the previous product and these are more active or toxic than the previous product, the apparatus must be analysed individually."	SOP-001153-6

"Validation protocol 
(similar to validation plan)"	"Term from ""Good Manufacturing Practice Guidelines, Part II"":
A written plan that specifies how to perform a validation and defines acceptance criteria. The plan for a production process specifies, for example, the process equipment, critical process parameters/operating ranges, product properties, samplings, test data to be recorded, the number of validation runs, and the acceptable test results.
The terms derived from this, ""Process Performance Qualification Protocol"" (PPQ Protocol) and ""Process Performance Qualification Report"" (PPQ Report), are used as equivalents to the traditional designations, ""Process Validation Plan"" and ""Process Validation Report"", and to the term, ""Process Qualification Plan and Report""."
